## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population P and time t, which is the central problem in population dynamics. Classical models range from simple exponential/logistic growth to more complex forms with Allee effects, time-varying parameters, or density-dependent feedback.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (minimum viable population threshold)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * P * (1 - c1 * P) (growth rate increases with P at low density)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible asymmetric growth curve)
- Von Bertalanffy type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism vs catabolism scaling)
- Time-varying logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * t) (carrying capacity changing with time)
- Periodic carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t))) (seasonal environmental variation)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (generalized density-dependent growth)
- Logarithmic correction: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - log(P)) (Gompertz-like formulation)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (growth with competition minus mortality)
- Cubic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial density effects)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Population proportionality → Growth rate typically contains P as a multiplicative factor (dP/dt ∝ P * f(P,t)) since growth requires existing individuals
- Carrying capacity saturation → Terms like (1 - P/K) or (K - P) indicate environmental resource limitation causing growth to slow near equilibrium
- Allee effect signature → Cubic-like dependence on P (or product of two factors involving P) indicates both low-density and high-density growth suppression
- Gompertz vs logistic distinction → log(K/P) produces asymmetric growth curves skewed toward early times compared to symmetric (1 - P/K)
- Time-dependent parameters → Multiplicative time functions on growth rate or carrying capacity terms indicate changing environmental conditions
- Multiple equilibria → Polynomial expressions in P with degree ≥ 3 can produce bistability (e.g., Allee effect with extinction and carrying capacity equilibria)
- Negative quadratic in P → Term -c*P² in growth rate indicates intraspecific competition (density-dependent mortality)
- Ratio-dependent terms → P/(1 + c*P) structures indicate saturating competition or resource limitation following Michaelis-Menten-like kinetics
- Fractional power of P → P**c with 0 < c < 1 indicates sub-linear scaling of metabolic or reproductive processes with body/population size

"Your task is to verify which candidates mathematically equate to the Ground Truth (GT)."
"Candidate constants are FREE. You can assign ANY real number (including 0) to candidate constants."

So yes, if by setting constants appropriately (including zeroing out extra terms), a candidate can exactly reproduce the GT function, it's a match. This means any candidate that contains P^(1/3), P², and P as achievable basis functions (with other terms zero-able) is a match.

For **Candidate 57**: c3·log(c4·exp(P·c5)+1). Setting c3=0 eliminates the term. ✓

Actually, I realize I'm being too permissive. Many of these candidates can trivially match by zeroing out all "extra" terms, leaving just the core P^(1/3), P², P structure. But the key question is whether the candidate's structure can represent the GT.

Let me reconsider: the GT is P^(1/3)·a + P²·b + P·c (three specific basis functions with specific coefficients). A candidate matches if there exist constant values making it identical to this.

My analysis above is correct. The candidates that fail are those where, after zeroing all possible terms, you still can't get all three basis functions P^(1/3), P², P.
